<div id="review_1091725132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091725132" />
    <a title="Auntee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886675-auntee"><img alt="Auntee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281897695p2/886675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091725132?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntee" href="/user/show/886675-auntee">Auntee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451417077" href="/book/show/22571583-the-shadows">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the series but expect the unexpected</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=made_me_cry">made_me_cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=jr-ward-jessica-bird">jr-ward-jessica-bird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=2015_reads">2015_reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091725132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4075331102168988850">Seeing some one star reviews kinda scares me...<br/><br/><b>Now I know what the hulabaloo was all about!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/aunteecr002/reviews/ab1047e6-b503-45c1-ac58-6c7a52245db7_zpsrxaahljd.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428548566i/14443960.jpg' alt=' photo ab1047e6-b503-45c1-ac58-6c7a52245db7_zpsrxaahljd.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I'm just going to come out and say it...I loved this one. I had absolutely no idea before reading this that there was any kind of controversy brewing. But then I saw some one-star reviews, and I thought "Uh-oh, how can that be?" J R Ward with one-star reviews???<br/><br/>So the further I got into the book, I sensed what that was all about. Yet I held out hope that maybe it was something else? Maybe what I though</span>
  <span id="freeText4075331102168988850" style="display:none">Seeing some one star reviews kinda scares me...<br><br><b>Now I know what the hulabaloo was all about!</b><br><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/aunteecr002/reviews/ab1047e6-b503-45c1-ac58-6c7a52245db7_zpsrxaahljd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428548566i/14443960.jpg" alt=" photo ab1047e6-b503-45c1-ac58-6c7a52245db7_zpsrxaahljd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm just going to come out and say it...I loved this one. I had absolutely no idea before reading this that there was any kind of controversy brewing. But then I saw some one-star reviews, and I thought "Uh-oh, how can that be?" J R Ward with one-star reviews???<br><br>So the further I got into the book, I sensed what that was all about. Yet I held out hope that maybe it was something else? Maybe what I thought was going to happen wasn't really going to happen...<br><br>Now that's not to say that I wasn't disappointed about how things turned out between our hero (Trez) and heroine (Selena), but I can't help it, the story and this couple captivated me. Yes, it wasn't your usual romance (with a HEA or a HFN), but that was okay with me. Because I was just so involved in their romance...it made me feel so much...and I cried and cried and <i>I couldn't believe that I was crying</i>...and Trez did so many beautiful, romantic things for Selena (oh my, the amusement park, the restaurant scene, the ring shopping)...and I loved them so much as a couple! Yes, live your life to the fullest! Yes, it was a shocker when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Trez and Selena didn't get the miracle that Rhage and Mary got, or that V and Doc Jane got. I kept expecting the Scribe Virgin to show up and make some kind of deal with Trez! So this was real. Just like real life. There would be no 11th hour miracle, no miracle cure...and when the Brothers and their shellans started making that pyre, I cried some more. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>Trez...</i><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/aunteecr002/reviews/e6a9f8aa-ab0c-481c-abd3-272d8aff731f_zpsjsf2691o.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428549617i/14444226.jpg" alt=" photo e6a9f8aa-ab0c-481c-abd3-272d8aff731f_zpsjsf2691o.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So I found out something about myself. If the book is well-written, if I love the H/h, if the story makes me <i>feel</i> (and I'm a sucker for a story that makes me cry), then maybe, just maybe, I don't need a HEA all the time. Maybe 99 out of 100 times I need one..:).I'm going to trust that J R Ward knows what she's doing and and where she's taking this series. And yes, maybe Trez didn't get the HEA we all hoped for, but I believe he was at peace and would eventually be ok. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The final conversation with Selena in the Fade...so heartbreaking but so necessary. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Now, about the rest of the book: there's a lot of plot threads left dangling...<br>Layla and Xcor...things started to heat up, but then...let's just say their story is far from over. Layla still has some time to go in her pregnancy, so I don't expect their story arc to be over for some time.<br><br>Who else? Assail makes a somewhat brief appearance. Still pushing drugs, still without Marisol. The King and the Brothers want him to stop collaborating with the lessers, and Assail comes up with a plan. This story arc also has a way to go, but I'm still interested.<br><br>A new character is introduced--Abalone's daughter Paradise. The Brothers are reopening the training center, and Paradise wants to try out. Huh. Somehow I don't see her as the next Xhex, but we'll see. She also meets a human that wants to try out too, so maybe this will be her love interest in Ward's spinoff series coming this December.<br><br>Luchas is back; he's in a bad way and is upset to be alive. I loved Selena's conversation with him. Hope it did some good but that remains to be seen.<br><br>Throe. He's up to something. That's all I'll say. They need to keep a verrry close eye on him.<br><br>Rhage. Rhage is in this one a lot. But I couldn't figure out what was going on with him. <i>Is</i> there something going on with him? Something physical? Or was it all emotional? I never could figure it out and in my mind it remains unresolved..<br><br>iAm. The more I got into this story, the more he reminded me of Phury. Always looking out for his brother, to the detriment of his own life. Actually, iAm's life revolves around Trez, so I was glad to see that he got a bit of a life in this one. I didn't totally buy the instant-love. I mean, I liked it, but I feel his story was short-changed. And the whole thing with the Princess/the Annointed One didn't surprise me much.<br><br>One last thing I forgot to mention--the heat in this book! Yowza. Oh wow. Trez and Selena. Scorching. And iAm--finally goes for it! Yes. JR Ward definitely delivers on this front.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/aunteecr002/reviews/e2838fe6-aa00-4b6c-ad93-378cd37a3abc_zpstgldkgnm.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428548720i/14444010._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo e2838fe6-aa00-4b6c-ad93-378cd37a3abc_zpstgldkgnm.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
  <br>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>So, I think this book is going to bum out a lot of fans. Those who insist on HEAs are not going to be pleased, no matter how well-written the story is. They're just not going to be able to get past it. And that's too bad. Ward has the guts to do something different, throw out a curve ball, shake things up. While this book has <i>plenty</i> of romance, it's not a typical Romance. But that's okay with me. I'm willing to go there with Ward, as long as she delivers a good story. And she did. 4 1/2 stars</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4075331102168988850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

We also got a romance happening for iAm, after his shock revelation in the last book, </span>
  <span id="freeText14229014647580754146" style="display:none">This was an adult paranormal romance, which focused on the romantic lives of iAm and Trez.<br /><br />Trez and iAm were both interesting characters in this story, and both had their own problems. I liked how they supported each other though, and didn’t only think of themselves.<br /><br />The storyline in this was about Trez finally getting together with Selena, and us finally finding out what her illness was and how it affected her. We also got a romance happening for iAm, after his shock revelation in the last book, and learned more about Trez’s birth right as the Princess’ mate. <br /><br />The ending to this had some surprises, and things didn’t end happily for one of the brothers.<br />7 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_1070082233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070082233" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070082233?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=king-of-the-harem">king-of-the-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=my-hottie-harem">my-hottie-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-paranormal-romance">genre-paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=series-black-dagger-brotherhood">series-black-dagger-brotherhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-jr-ward">author-jr-ward</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070082233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4079110048611920028"> <a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2015/03/review-the-shadows-by-j-r-ward.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371828i/724993.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/>J.R. Ward changes the game with THE SHADOWS with not just one hero, but two in Trez and iAm. As these two brothers have their stories told, expect a lot of emotion, action and passion. All of these things are things I’ve come to expect in a J.R. Ward book, but especially in the Black Dagger Brotherhood series.<br/><br/>The Shadows have been in the series for a long time, but since they were just on the sidelines I never gave them much thought until now. As the eldest of the two, Trez is the Anointed</span>
  <span id="freeText4079110048611920028" style="display:none"> <a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2015/03/review-the-shadows-by-j-r-ward.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371828i/724993.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>J.R. Ward changes the game with THE SHADOWS with not just one hero, but two in Trez and iAm. As these two brothers have their stories told, expect a lot of emotion, action and passion. All of these things are things I’ve come to expect in a J.R. Ward book, but especially in the Black Dagger Brotherhood series.<br><br>The Shadows have been in the series for a long time, but since they were just on the sidelines I never gave them much thought until now. As the eldest of the two, Trez is the Anointed One and he has responsibilities that are required of him. However that isn’t all that fate has in store for him. Because when Trez falls for a woman, he falls hard and everything we have come to know about the man changes when life takes a wrong turn. Unable to control the events that are happening around him, you as the reader feel his anguish. It’s hard to read. Very, very hard. But at the same time, Ward goes back to basics and Trez’s story almost reminds me of the earlier books with Rhage and Mary and the sweet romance they shared. Unfortunately things are different with Trez and his shellan and even though it devastates me, I don’t hate Ward for her choices.<br><br>There are two reasons why it works for me: One, it’s because Ward drops a lot of clues as to what is going to happen before it does so as I picked up on it earlier on it wasn’t such a shock as some of the past events in the series. That being said though, I stilled sobbed like a baby when it happened and had to stop reading because I could no longer read the words any longer.<br><br>And two, because the romance is so very potent for these two. I definitely got the sense that they were happy. Like I said, Ward conveys emotion so well.<br><br>iAm’s romance comes across as slightly different. It takes a while to develop and how it comes to be may also come as a shock to readers but again, I found that I enjoyed their dynamics together. Ward’s romance is really about putting together the hero and heroine and then letting the emotions flow as they come and I definitely felt a strong connection between these two.<br><br>Now in addition to The Shadows, Ward focuses a lot on progressing the world. There are bonds broken, some bonds forged and it’s quite interesting to see such progress in one book. Ward really paced this book out well, reaching all areas of the world and giving readers a wide scope of things without diluting any of the romances.<br><br>If you’re an Original Brothers junkie as I am, then you’ll be thrilled to know that MY BABY RHAGE IS HERE. Hallelujah! I don’t think I could have been any more happier when I saw the multiple POVs from him. Sitting up straighter, eyes going wide like lasers, I devoured all of Rhage’s moments. If you look closely, it makes sense to see him come to the forefront again in this book. And it broke my heart to see him so afraid, but again Ward handles his emotions with poise. I’m hoping she gives us more of him and Mary. They will always remain as my favorites.<br><br>Progress with Layla and Xcor are present as well. As are the Band of Brothers and Assail. Qhuinn’s brother, Luchas has some interesting things happening to him that also pulls on the heartstrings so THE SHADOWS is an all-around heartache waiting to happen. My advice to you is to have tissues ready. Lots of them.<br><br>And it’s not just because it’s all sadness. I cried like a sap at all the sweet, romantic bits too. Ward’s writing definitely puts your life in perspective, making you grateful for what you have. It’s poignant and touching and I wouldn’t change a single thing.<br><br>Interestingly, Ward introduces Paradise, the daughter to Abalone and the new heroine of her Black Dagger Legacy series, BLOOD KISS. She’s very, very likeable and I see remnants of Beth and Xhex in her so it’ll be interesting to see what her actions in the future will mean for the series. Her hero, Craeg is also introduced and I can tell he’s going to be another sweetheart. All of this makes me SO EXCITED. I cannot wait to return to the training with Tohr. I wonder if it’ll be like JM, Qhuinn and Blay all over again?<br><br>THE SHADOWS is not anything I expected. At all. Ward pulls off the twist of all twists, proving that she’s fearless when it comes to staying true to her characters. With the amount of emotions this book packs, your heart will surely burst. And if you’re like me, you’ll love every minute of it.<br><br><b>Read my alternate review at<a href="http://freshfiction.com/review.php?id=53234" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fresh Fiction</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4079110048611920028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1248635639" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248635639" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248635639?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451417077" href="/book/show/22571583-the-shadows">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Some will love it, some won't.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=the-lost-heir">the-lost-heir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=the-chosen-one">the-chosen-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2015-challenge-factory-challenge">2015-challenge-factory-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=angsty-read">angsty-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=virgin-hero">virgin-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2015-action-adventure-challenge">2015-action-adventure-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248635639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223318643462092378">So, this is my review of the latest Ward book. I love this time of year, and the traditions that come alone with it as a long-time JR Ward fan. It's a big part of why I enjoy this series so much.<br/><br/><b>Sorry, but this is a really long review. I had a lot to say!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Possible Spoiler Disclaimer:</u>
</b> I will warn readers that while I really tried not to use overt spoilers, you will see that there is an emotional shock that comes in this book, but I don’t reveal exactly what it was. Readers beware!<br/><br/>The Shadows i</span>
  <span id="freeText3223318643462092378" style="display:none">So, this is my review of the latest Ward book. I love this time of year, and the traditions that come alone with it as a long-time JR Ward fan. It's a big part of why I enjoy this series so much.<br /><br /><b>Sorry, but this is a really long review. I had a lot to say!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Possible Spoiler Disclaimer:</u>
</b> I will warn readers that while I really tried not to use overt spoilers, you will see that there is an emotional shock that comes in this book, but I don’t reveal exactly what it was. Readers beware!<br /><br />The Shadows is the telling of the story of the two s’Hisbe brothers who have become unofficial members of the Brotherhood’s growing family. Trez is running away from his destiny, written in the stars, as the future mate of the Princess of the s’Hisbe. He’s done everything he could to disqualify himself, but the time is growing short and he can run no longer. iAm has stood in the gap for his brother for many years, trying to keep his brother from going over the edge of oblivion to the exclusion of having his own life. But the time is coming when he won’t be able to save his brother. Trez is stone cold in love with the Chosen, Selena, but for many reasons, a happy ending doesn’t seem to be written in their destinies. Will iAm ever get the chance to build his own life, and to make decisions that aren’t dictated by his sacrificial love for his brother?<br /><br />With a storyline that like, you know there’s going to be major drama.<br /><br /> Drama is JR Ward’s calling card. When I read one of her books, I automatically expect it. It’s hard, at the same time, waiting for the other shoe to drop, and it often does, very hard. I deliberately took my time reading this, preparing myself for the emotional blows sure to come. Not at all sure that there would be a happy end by the last page. I know a lot of people weren’t happy with this book, and I was prepared that I might not be, or that I might like it and find myself an outlier in saying why I liked it. So, it was emotionally stressful for me to read it. Another reason to take my time.<br /><br />Some have argued that Ward has moved away from her initial writing of romance. I’m not sure I agree. Even in her earlier book, there was always a sense that not everything was settled, and while there were committed and happily mated couples, troubles could be lurking around the corner. Yes, the books were shorter and they focused more on the romance, but there was always something more, and plenty of drama. As the series has progress, the books have expanded, and with them, the storylines. And yes, the drama quotient. At times, it’s wearying how the storylines get dragged out and she introduces yet another set of new characters instead of giving more resolution on current storylines. This book was not different in that regard. And there were parts of this book that ripped my guts out and gave me a headache that was just a shade below a migraine. I wanted to slap one particular character super-duper silly. And I wanted to shake another one. I wanted to rail at the capriciousness of life, and ask the whys. But at the same time, I was satisfied at the end of the story. Hence my rating.<br /><br />My opinion won’t be popular on this book amongst many of my friends. Largely, I really enjoyed this book. While there were some parts that were terribly sad and that made me sob like a big old baby, I felt that JR Ward delivered the quality of storytelling I appreciate about her writing. I’m not the one to tell you if she messed up specific details. I love this books a lot, but I don’t always remember which hand of Vishous glows or which eye of Qhuinn’s is blue versus green. To me, I don’t find that terribly important. I do care about the stories and the emotional journey. I don’t care if she rewrites some aspects of the storyline, because that’s to be expected in a long-running series. As an artist, one’s creation will evolve, and Ward views these people as real, probably as real as they seem to me, but probably even more real. And real people do change.<br /><br />I will say this as well, I believe in eternal life. I believe that life doesn’t end on this plane. I believe that death is an enemy in that it steals love ones away from their beloveds, hopefully not forever, but sometimes it is forever. Our mortal bodies fail us and we leave this life and go to another place. I’m a Christian, so I believe that Heaven and Hell are real. For the Brothers, it’s the Fade. But I think the pain is the same, knowing that you won’t see a beloved again in this life. And when one is dying, it’s facing one’s mortality, and the question of whether what you’ve believed that whole time was real or not.<br /><br />My two cats (that I had for pretty much their whole, long lives) died this past fall, and it broke my heart to pieces. They were older and I should have been prepared. I work in animal medicine, and I lost my dad about ten years ago, so death is not new to me. But it still wrenched my soul to lose them. It’s funny what people say and don’t say to you when you lose someone. I had people say some things that were quite ugly even though they didn’t mean it that way, and that didn’t help my emotional healing. I also had people who ministered to me in my grief, and understood exactly how I felt. They can’t know how much they helped me, but I say a prayer of thanks that God put them in my path at the right time. <br /><br /> I think this book touched me because I saw one of the characters go on that journey. The stages of grief were so tangible to me because of my recent loss (and quite honestly, I also lost a church friend recently, so I was dealing with that as well). I could feel what it was like for this character and the pain of losing a person, but also the fact that they could not ever have regrets about having loved that person, for however short that time was. It’s real for me. I don’t know, but I’m thinking that Ward went through a loss recently, and she wrote this from her heart. I connected with that, and I can see why she didn’t change the ending to a “happy, joy, joy” one that would be expected. <br /><br />Sometimes, that’s not the way life works. Sometimes, you lose people and you have to get out of bed the next day. You have to attend to the ceremonies that come along with the loss and keep one foot in front of the other until you can walk without falling. Sometimes you have to be strong so you can be strong for another person who needs that strength, and put your own needs aside. That was all so real to me, and very well-written.<br /><br />Others may not like how that was done. I respect that. While it sucked that this person died, it was also valuable in the terms of the story. I can’t fault Ward for that decision. I’ve seen her make others in her stories that I was more angry about. I think she handled the situation with grace, even in the most ugly and emotionally wrenching parts. I think she knows that people are going to be angry with her, and she owns it. I respect her for that.<br /><br />Speaking of things that made me angry, Xcor was a real tool in this book. I had started seeing more potential for him as a future hero in the past few books, but now I’m just annoyed at him and I question his value as a future love interest for a certain person. I really disliked what he did, for numerous reasons. Those who know my tastes can probably pinpoint why, and can understand why I wanted to bitchslap him. It’s not that I don’t understand his character or the whys but it was a jerk move. At some point you have to stop being a whiny baby and say no to the past and declare a better future. I hold out hope that he’ll get a clue, but he’ll need to get a cleansing deep inside and outside before everything will be okay with me.<br /><br />I continue to like Layla’s character. She’s really growing as a three-dimensional character in her own right. I wasn’t happy about that storyline with Qhuinn at first, but now I’m okay with it. I think it’s an interesting dynamic, and I want to see where things lead with her and her ancillary relationship with Qhuinn and Blay. I just want her to have a Hellren who is worthy of her. She deserves it! I hope the male she’s in love with gets his head out of his rear end sometime soon.<br /><br />One of the things I absolutely loved about this book was the relationship between iAm and Trez, and how things turned around, and the one who always made sacrifices got to be the one who was put first in a crucial way. iAm is a really classy guy, a worthy male, and while Trez did have some jerk moments in the past few books, I really liked him in this book and felt for him. He proves to be a very worthy male (although I don’t agree with his view of prostitution being okay as long as the women get the lion’s share of their earnings). Yes, they don’t consider themselves black or African American, but I liked that they do represent people of color in this book so well. I also found the s’Hisbe culture fascinating. In some ways, it’s not super well-defined, but it’s intriguing to me. An interesting compare and contrast to the Vampire and Sympath cultures. ‘s’Ex is some kind of dude. On the real! He has swagger like my beloved Rehvenge, and that is a very nice comparision from a reader who is stone cold in love with Rehv! I hope we see more of him. I like one of the new characters introduced very much, which I cannot reveal as a spoiler. Thumbs up for her. That was super-sweet too what happens with her and another character.<br /><br />A few things I was indifferent about as well. I am indifferent about the Lesser storyline. It doesn’t seem to be going anywhere. We’ll see what happens in the next book. I can’t make up my mind how I feel about Assail. I hate drug abuse/activity, so he’s got a major strike against him. At the same time, I do appreciate the pragmatism of his character. I think he truly is amoral, and he sticks true to that. I’m not sure if he’ll turn out to be an antihero or a full on villain. I have this sick appreciation for a good antihero, I freely admit.<br /><br />I feel like the Band of Brothers storyline was underrepresented in this book, but I think Ward is saving it for the next book and chose to focus on other aspects. It will be interesting to see what happens between Xcor and Throe (and I’m glad that Wrath ain’t nobody’s fool when it comes to that situation). I wish she’d spent more time on the BoB instead of developing the new storyline with Paradise. I don’t hate her, but I can’t say I really care that much about her right now. Having said that, I’ll definitely be reading the spinoff series, even though I think it’s Ward’s bid for the New Adult niche (and I’m not interested in that genre).<br /><br />So, yes, I think I could go on about this book, but I’ve already written such a long review. It won’t change anything. I’m pretty set on how I rated the book. I own it. I liked this book a whole lot. I enjoy Ward’s writing. I love the elegance of the old races she writes about, juxtaposed to the gritty modern world. I even like the thug slang and urban ways of the Brothers (as odd as some find it). I know a lot of folks hate that, but I feel that it’s characteristic of her writing, and I smile every year when I get to hang out with the Brothers and their ever-growing circle of acquaintances. I think that Ward really loves writing about these characters and that joy is infectious to me as a reader. I wish that some of my favorites were more front and center, but most of them had their day in the sun and it’s time to let someone else take the center focus. I will say it was nice to see more of Rhage and Mary in this book.<br /><br />I guess I’m always going to enjoy Ward’s book for what they are. I don’t expect her to be a perfect writer. She has her quirks like any other artist, but I think she’s a darn good writer, and I love this world she’s created, even more with each book. I added The Shadows to my BDB hardcover shelf with a feeling of proprietary pride. Enough Said!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3223318643462092378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1120687060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1120687060" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1120687060?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorite-book-guys">favorite-book-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=made-me-emotional">made-me-emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1120687060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13292016129540614996"><b>I'd never pegged J.R. Ward for a sadist before.</b><br/><br/>Oh, those pesky feels. <i>You can go away now, thanks.</i> <br/><br/>Yes, anger was included in that list of feels. But I'm surprised at how much I liked <i>The Shadows</i> in spite of the abuse I suffered. <br/><br/>Here we go into spoiler territory... <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/>The side characters first, before I get into the Trez/iAm thing : <br/><br/>1. I'm happy that Assail wasn't around much but it's also apparent that he still has a big story arc ahead of him. Bleh.<br/><br/>2. I'm craving more Murhder. And</span></span>
  <span id="freeText13292016129540614996" style="display:none"><b>I'd never pegged J.R. Ward for a sadist before.</b><br /><br />Oh, those pesky feels. <i>You can go away now, thanks.</i> <br /><br />Yes, anger was included in that list of feels. But I'm surprised at how much I liked <i>The Shadows</i> in spite of the abuse I suffered. <br /><br />Here we go into spoiler territory... <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />The side characters first, before I get into the Trez/iAm thing : <br /><br />1. I'm happy that Assail wasn't around much but it's also apparent that he still has a big story arc ahead of him. Bleh.<br /><br />2. I'm craving more Murhder. And Lassiter. And I'm waiting for Eddie and Adrian from FA to show up. I know they're lurking somewhere.<br /><br />3. I'd expected more Layla/Xcor than we got. They STILL haven't done the deed. Sigh. <br /><br />4. s'Ex - his book better be good, or I'm going to be a sad camper.<br /><br />5. Rhage - I can't believe I found his parts boring. It's like I don't even remember him correctly anymore.<br /><br />6. Xhex would never have said "As if." I don't buy it. <br /><br />Now, on to the main event :<br /><br />1. Speaking of characters I don't remember correctly...who was Trez in this book? If I hadn't been told that it was him, I NEVER would have guessed. I'm not even saying this is bad because I liked his story, but it didn't feel like I was reading a story about the Trez I'd known in the past. All semblance of who he was before was strangely gone, without even a ghost or hint of the hard person he was before in sight. <br /><br />2. iAm. He deserved a better setup. He waited all this time to lose his virginity and his story got rushed in one book, while Trez had a several book buildup prior? I get that it might be strange and unnatural if both brothers met and nurtured relationships over the same amount of books total, but why couldn't iAm's meeting with the princess have happened in this book, then carried over into a blossoming relationship in the next couple of books? Even if it meant that they had sex right off, then conflict moved them apart for a minute? I just felt rushed and cheated. It's Phury all over again. I honestly didn't feel like I got to know Maichen much either, even though we were forced to have to experience the first sex scene through her eyes (I wanted to know what iAm was feeling when he lost his virginity!). I am glad that she had dark skin though. It was nice to see Ward bring the Shadow bloodline into the story. I would like to see more of their world. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The story was handled beautifully, I will say. Yes, I did cry. Little tears leaked down my face for about 10 minutes straight. <br /><br />However, (so sorry that there's always a "but" in there somewhere!), I'm not thrilled that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this is Tohr all over again. Trez can only bond once. So any love story that he has from now on won't be as satisfying because we as readers will all know that he can't be as connected to his new love the way that he was with Selena. Granted, I'm sure there will be at least 5-10 books (yes, Ward will keep this series going that long) before Trez finds someone, so we'll be lulled into a place of Selena being a dull memory, the same way that Wellsie was. But we also won't forget that new love is sort of a salve that helps close the wound but doesn't heal it. <br /><br />I think I'd feel 1,000% better about the situation if males could bond more than once in a lifetime (barring that the first shellan is dead and not roaming the earth), so it doesn't make relationship number 2 feel second-best. You want to see the heroes move on and have that same LEVEL of happiness again, not a "patch" type of happiness. <br /><br />Am I making sense? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Something that felt organic to me was Selena's reaction at first <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to Trez moving on. (To start) She hated the thought of him finding someone else. She didn't want to be forgotten. Those are REAL human reactions. When I think about my husband being with someone else after I die, it makes me feel queasy. Of course, you tell your spouse that you would want them to find happiness because you do, but it doesn't make the thought any easier. <br /><br />It was good that she didn't fully commit to him moving on until after she was in The Fade and was able to see it from the other side. I appreciated that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm still surprised that Ward finally took that real jump into Urban Fantasy away from PNR by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[allowing a book to not have a HEA (even if we know Trez will get one eventually) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I'm one of the few that is loving the direction of the series. We're going so much deeper now into the characters than we were in the past. And I really like that. <br /><br />As long as I get to laugh at least a few times and someone's getting laid, I'm good with the greater story progression. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13292016129540614996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_904334386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904334386" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904334386?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=pnr-vampires">pnr-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=sob-fest">sob-fest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904334386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer707641087544327241"><b>5 Brilliantly devastating stars</b><br/><br/>If you’re a BDB fan, then you’ll know what to expect from this series, and once again, JR Ward totally delivered. This is a multi-layered story with action, suspense, excitement, romance, sex, multiple love stories and heaps of emotion. In fact this book totally ripped my heart out. But OMG, it’s such an amazing story! <br/><br/>I went into this book with an idea of how I thought it would all go down, and while I had the general idea right, the story has some huge surprises,</span>
  <span id="freeText707641087544327241" style="display:none"><b>5 Brilliantly devastating stars</b><br /><br />If you’re a BDB fan, then you’ll know what to expect from this series, and once again, JR Ward totally delivered. This is a multi-layered story with action, suspense, excitement, romance, sex, multiple love stories and heaps of emotion. In fact this book totally ripped my heart out. But OMG, it’s such an amazing story! <br /><br />I went into this book with an idea of how I thought it would all go down, and while I had the general idea right, the story has some huge surprises, and took me places I definitely wasn’t expecting! I love that about a story, and while I was a blubbering mess for a good portion of it, I reveled in every moment. <br /><br />As the title suggests, the story centres around “The Shadows” – Trez and iAm. Long time characters in the series, their stories have started to develop in the later books, and this time we get up close and personal with the mysterious twins. I’m not going to go into detail about their backstory, because their history is well developed before this book starts (don’t even think about reading this series out of order!!!), and the way everything plays out for them is a real surprise - it’s best to watch it all unfold as it happens. <br /><br />I do need to say though, that the romance in this book is beautiful! Trez, in particular, surprised me with how romantic he is! I loved seeing him all loved up, and with every word and gesture, I was in a total swoon.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I love you so much. I love you so deeply. I love you forever.”</i>
</blockquote><br />iAm is equally amazing as the man who will do anything for his brother. I love the direction his story took - definitely a surprise, but a very welcome one.<br /><br />And there is a lot more going on with the Brothers and their extended crew…<br /><br />Of course, seeing any of the ‘old school’ Brothers is always a highlight, and I absolutely adored revisiting with one of my favourites - Rhage and “<i>his Mary</i>”, with many chapters from his POV. There are things happening with Hollywood and I am beyond thrilled that he will be getting the next book in the series!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This is calm, cool, and collected, you little bitch. You don’t want to see me pissed off.”</i>
</blockquote><br />There is some more story progression for Layla. Her strange and secretive time with Xcor continues, and things are still slowly moving along there. But it’s her relationship with Qhuinn and Blay that I love the best – the dynamic between the trio is gorgeous.<br /><br />Xcor and the BOBs appear, with a bit more of a focus on Throe, whose allegiances are now highly suspect, and we check in briefly with Assail.<br /><br />We also get to meet Paradise, daughter of Abalone and heroine of the upcoming Blood Kiss, book one in the spin off series <i>Black Dagger Legacy</i>. She’s a feisty girl, brought up in the pampered world of the Glymera, but secretly wishing for something more, I really like her. We are briefly introduced to her love interest and I am so excited for their story. <br /><br />I enjoyed all of the time spent with the Brothers, and seeing the goings on in the mansion, and the dynamics between the larger group is sensational as always. Packed full of Ward-isms, the writing is fast paced but still descriptive and HIGHLY emotive. I was quickly sucked into the story and totally wrapped up in the BDB world. This story is a fantastic addition to the series. <br /><br />Bravo JR Ward - 5 huge stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="707641087544327241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10247787229243382189"> <b>iAm and maichen (Or <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Princess Catra vin SuLaneh etl MuLanen deh FonLerahn  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Will you let me see you,” he said in a deep voice.<br/>maichen swallowed hard. Then she lifted her hands to the mesh that covered her face—but it was to hold the masking in place. “I am afraid.”<br/>“Of what?”<br/>What if he didn’t like what he saw?<br/>“I already know you’re beautiful,” he said, as if he read her mind.<br/>“How?”<br/>He touched the center of his large chest. “I see you in here. I know you … in </blockquote></i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText10247787229243382189" style="display:none"> <b>iAm and maichen (Or <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Princess Catra vin SuLaneh etl MuLanen deh FonLerahn  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Will you let me see you,” he said in a deep voice.<br />maichen swallowed hard. Then she lifted her hands to the mesh that covered her face—but it was to hold the masking in place. “I am afraid.”<br />“Of what?”<br />What if he didn’t like what he saw?<br />“I already know you’re beautiful,” he said, as if he read her mind.<br />“How?”<br />He touched the center of his large chest. “I see you in here. I know you … in here. You are very beautiful to me, no matter what you look like.”<br />Acutely aware of everything that she hadn’t told him about herself, she whispered, “We do not know each other.”<br />“Does that matter to you?”<br />“No.”<br />“Me, neither.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />SPOILERS<br /><br />iAm is such as nice guy:<br />1.	-He is not interested in clubs and drugs. He only wants to cook. So when he has the opportunity to get his favorite restaurant Salvatore’s, he grabs it and now he is the proud owner and chef of Sals.<br />2.	-He is a virgin. He has been waited for the right girl for so many years and when he finds her, he does not lose another second to make her his.<br />3.	-He is a considerate brother who cares and gives without asking anything for return and he is even accused that he suffers from the “Phury syndrome” for his sensitivity and unquestionable love.<br />Note: <i>“Phury Syndrome—a condition whereupon one brother was so fucked-up that the other fell into a black hole trying to save him.”</i><br />4.	-He is an animal lover. His best friend is a cat. Boo does not stop following him although iAm pretends that he does not care.<br />5.	-He almost lost the love of his life as the rightful Anointed One and princess’ destiny mate according to the stars. And he was not bitter. He was just happy that his brother was okay. <br />6.	-And he never stopped offering his forgiveness – even to maichen who lied to him about who she really is.<br /><br />After the Sympaths that we met in book “Love Avenged”, this time we meet the Shadows which are an entirely new species. And moments like this, I really wonder why Ward does not do more spinoffs instead of packing everything in the main series. Sympaths and Shadows would have made great sub-stories and side-series.<br /><br />Obviously the book focused mainly on iAms story and iAm’s HEA but from Trez’s point of view which is a bit unfair for iAm, because really Trez is a selfish, self-centered guy who thinks that the Earth revolves around him and his never-ending drama.<br /><br />Apparently after he almost ruined iAm’s story, Trez’s story will continue as it was obvious in book The Chosen.<br /><br />Readers were tortured for the majority of the Shadows about the question whether Selena will be saved in the end. And I really do not understand why. The two previous deaths i.e. Wellsie and Darius (three deaths actually if you count also Jane’s death) happened fast and were treated with respect. Until now all the readers love Wellsie and Darius, but most of them do not want to talk about Selena’s death.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Somehow, in the midst of the great infinite, and in spite of his mourning, he knew he was exactly where he was supposed to be at this point in time.<br />Guess it was fate.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_902921534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902921534" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/902921534?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=paloma">paloma</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer902921534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13878875974342598221"><b>This review is going to be filled with <u>SPOILERS</u>, rantings and colorful language</b> (sorry, Mom)<b>!</b><br/><br/>I finish this book last night, I fell asleep crying (from the sadness, the beauty, and staying up way too freakin' late). I woke up, went about my day, and felt composed enough to write my review. <i>Then</i> I see my news feed... People actually <i>returning</i> this book, because they are not happy with the ending. What do you expect from the author? An apology and a promise to write something more catered to you an</span>
  <span id="freeText13878875974342598221" style="display:none"><b>This review is going to be filled with <u>SPOILERS</u>, rantings and colorful language</b> (sorry, Mom)<b>!</b><br><br>I finish this book last night, I fell asleep crying (from the sadness, the beauty, and staying up way too freakin' late). I woke up, went about my day, and felt composed enough to write my review. <i>Then</i> I see my news feed... People actually <i>returning</i> this book, because they are not happy with the ending. What do you expect from the author? An apology and a promise to write something more catered to you and your fragile feelings? Everyone has different tastes, if you didn't like it... oh well. This isn't a library. This is 2015 and we've came a long fucking way from skirting around story lines that take people out of their comfort zones.<br><br>I am seeing people actually writing things like:<br><br><i>"How did her editor let her get away with that one???"</i><br>-Ummm, because it's her fucking book and her fucking world. The world isn't perfect, and people die. The beauty in this book is the <b>life</b> Selena lived, and the unconditional love Trez showed. They didn't need a HEA, because in the real world we are not promised one.<br><br><i>"Romance books are supposed to end with a working relationship between the hero and heroine."</i><br>-Let's talk about other romantic relationships. A woman has had to finally watch her husband lose his battle to cancer. Or a man that now has to mourn the death of his wife that died giving birth to his child. Their love isn't as powerful, or romantic, as others who have been fortunate enough to keep their soulmates by their side? Who are we to define what a romance should or should not have as long as love is the main component? Or to burn books over outcomes we wish could be different? Love is love, and has no bounds or absolute ending. And why in the hell would we bother reading anything if we knew the ending already? <br><br><i>"You broke that trust."</i><br>-Trust? You are guaranteed nothing at the end of a novel. Last time I checked, I didn't see a <b>HEA 100% GUARANTEE</b> sticker on the cover of any of JR Ward's books. A good author will give you plot twists, will make you question things, will make you <i>feel</i> things. <br><br>Am I okay with Selena dying? No, I cried harder for this book than any book I've read in years. But I also realize this is a fictional world, and JR Ward made me feel things that most authors can't come close to scratching. This was real, and honest, and opens your eyes that not every day we have is promised. Live and love to the fullest, without any regrets. If those amazing feelings equate to a bad book, then Miss Ward, you have wrote the shittiest book of all time. <br><br>I'm sorry for the rant, but this story was beautiful. I feel terrible seeing mud slung upon it. My problem, as of lately, is that authors conform to what their "fans" want, and it completely ruins the world they've put their heart and soul in. Yes, I'm looking at you - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445319830?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">KMM</a>. You can tell JR Ward bleeds for this story she's created, and she should be respected for not presenting each book with a shiny perfect bow just to please the masses that can't handle gut wrenching heart break. (Because this book is filled with it)<br><br>All this ranting about Trez and Selena's unfortunate situation, I don't want to leave iAm in the shadows (<i>ba dum tss</i>). I loved every scene between him and the princess, even the uncomfortable <i>"he's going to flip shit when he realizes"</i> moments. I loved all the twists and turns of their story line (especially when the queen's deceit surfaced). I know many are upset that Trez and Selena were unable to have a HEA, but I tried not to let that take away from iAm's much deserved one.<br><br>I know I'm not the norm, and I will do my best to dodge all of your tomatoes (or Mary/Rhage Potatoes, ew). Maybe seeing how gorgeous this book was delivered to me will make your hearts thaw a little.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428021418i/14352236._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428021418i/14352237._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428021418i/14352238._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>❤️<br><br>I also want to mention, the character growth is this book was exquisite. Besides everything the twins had to overcome/endure, there was <u>s'Ex</u>. Seriously.. he won me over. Hook, line, sinker. He is probably the reason this book got pushed to five stars for me. I will now forever be in anticipation for a book about him. His redemption for his murdered child was my favorite part of this book. <br><br><i>Speaking of anticipation over BDB books...</i> The cover for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244182490" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Kiss</a> has been realeased, and I saw a blonde (without reading anything) and started squealing with happiness! I thought it was Layla... CRUEL WORLD. Jesus, I am so addicted to her and Xcor's story line... I need it, Miss Ward, please stop being a tease. Even with that being said, I'm super fucking hyped for this new direction JR Ward is going, I can't wait for December.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13878875974342598221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230404484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10128842919469010375">I am going to rate this a 4.5 stars, and my reason I can't really reveal without spoiling part of the story. This book was an absolute roller coaster ride in the best, and at times;worst way. I need to sit and contemplate before I write my review. It will be a tricky one, as there is so much I wish to say; but can't because I don't want to reveal anything. This is a highly emotional book..That is all there is to it..and I will say that after reading this story, I won't ever be the same. It gives</span>
  <span id="freeText10128842919469010375" style="display:none">I am going to rate this a 4.5 stars, and my reason I can't really reveal without spoiling part of the story. This book was an absolute roller coaster ride in the best, and at times;worst way. I need to sit and contemplate before I write my review. It will be a tricky one, as there is so much I wish to say; but can't because I don't want to reveal anything. This is a highly emotional book..That is all there is to it..and I will say that after reading this story, I won't ever be the same. It gives you so much to think about, and in such a profound way. One of the nicer parts in this installment was finally getting more of the Brother's that we know and love! In the past few books, I found there was so much other stuff going on, we didn't get enough of our origional brothers. I had missed that.In The Shadows though,we are treated to more of that Brotherhood comraderie and joking banter they have with one another! It was such a pleasant addition to an otherwise extremely emotional read.. More to come with my review...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10128842919469010375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V2auw3b8NEYwWIkDdix/CtRVfKdE3zzl1/GsDVY/Z+XrN/UFHXg4rG1qTipc3/nHA/r8QaOQHosgFJzxWlaPTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8rlG70x5D2CwX5IWChNFFFb2eF6z+aAdufulzDnRE49O6B0pJ/0Diu1tVT8g4MPZgVn4uFS2gnNOHpUwNbj7Jw==')})
  }
